## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics (classical mechanics)
**Analysis**: The task involves acceleration (dv/dt) as a function of position (x), velocity (v), and time (t) in a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. This belongs to classical mechanics, specifically the study of oscillatory systems where restoring forces may be nonlinear and damping or driving terms may be present. The physical relationships are governed by Newton's second law with position-dependent forces (spring-like), velocity-dependent forces (damping), and possibly explicit time-dependent driving.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear damping)
- Forced linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (sinusoidal driving)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring force with damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping depending on x^2)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear damping depending on v^3)
- Combined Duffing-Rayleigh: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (cubic restoring and cubic damping)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (asymmetric restoring force)
- Mathieu-type parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) + c3 * v (parametric excitation)
- Nonlinear pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (exact pendulum equation with damping)
- Softening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x / (1 + c1 * x**2) + c2 * v (saturating restoring force)
- General power-law restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * Abs(x)**c1 * sign(x) + c2 * v (arbitrary hardening/softening)
- Forced Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (driven cubic oscillator)
- Bistable oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (higher-order odd polynomial potential)
- Preloaded spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * Abs(x) + c2 * v (piecewise linear with offset)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Harmonic motion: acceleration proportional to negative position → linear term c0*x dominates, no higher powers
- Damping signature: presence of v terms (c1*v) indicates energy dissipation; linear damping gives exponential amplitude decay
- Hard spring effect: terms like x**3 with same sign as linear x term cause frequency increase with amplitude (Duffing hardening)
- Soft spring effect: saturating or sub-linear terms (x/(1+x**2), sin(x), |x|^c with c<1) cause frequency decrease with amplitude
- Self-sustained oscillation: nonlinear damping that changes sign (e.g., (1 - c*x**2)*v or v - c*v**3) indicates energy injection at small amplitudes and dissipation at large amplitudes
- Periodic driving: presence of sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) suggests external forcing, leading to resonance and possibly entrainment
- Parametric excitation: product of x with a time-periodic function (e.g., x*cos(c*t)) indicates driving via parameter modulation, enabling instability and half-frequency resonance
- Bistable potential: odd polynomial with alternating signs (e.g., -x + x**3) creates two stable equilibria, enabling switching dynamics
- Non-differentiable damping: terms like Abs(x), sign(v), or tanh(c*v) approximate dry friction or preloaded springs, giving stick-slip behavior
- Conservative system: absence of any v or t terms in dv/dt indicates energy conservation, leading to closed phase trajectories

GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*exp(-Abs(x))*v
Candidates evaluated: 64

The Ground Truth (GT) is `F0*sin(t) - beta*exp(-Abs(x))*v`, which simplifies to a linear combination of two independent basis functions: `sin(t)` and `v*exp(-Abs(x))`. The exact numerical constants are `F0 = 0.156062620221068` and `beta = 0.372947617362308`. The GT requires the exponential term to involve `Abs(x)` and not simply `x`.

We analyze each candidate to see if it can be made exactly equal to the GT by choosing its free constants (including setting extra terms to zero). The necessary ingredients are:
- A term that reduces to `A*sin(t)` (no dependence on `x` or `v`, frequency 1, zero phase). This can be achieved by `c*sin(c1 + c2*t)` with `c1=0, c2=1`, or by sums of such sines, or by `c*exp(c1*v)*sin(...)` with `c1=0`, etc.
- A term that reduces to `B*v*exp(C*Abs(x))` with `C < 0`. This must contain `v` linearly and `exp(c*Abs(x))`. Candidates without `Abs(x)` in the exponential (using `exp(c*x)`) cannot match because `x` can be negative and `exp(c*x)` ≠ `exp(c*Abs(x))` for all real `x`.
- All other additive terms must be capable of being exactly zeroed by setting their coefficients to zero.

Candidates that **lack** `Abs(x)` in the relevant exponential term: **8, 12, 18, 30, 36, 41, 42, 45, 56, 59, 63, 64**. These cannot match.

All other candidates (1–7, 9–11, 13–17, 19–29, 31–35, 37–40, 43–44, 46–55, 57–58, 60–62) contain a term of the form `c_i * v * exp(c_j * Abs(x))` and a sine term. Any additional terms (polynomials, extra exponentials, logarithms, rational functions, etc.) are additive, and their coefficients can be set to zero. For example, **Candidate 1** has an extra term `c5*exp(c6*sin(c7*t + c8))`; setting `c5 = 0` eliminates it entirely, leaving the required two terms. **Candidate 62** is exactly the required two terms with no extras.

Thus, numerous candidates can be algebraically reduced to the GT exactly.
